      "authorSolution": "\\( u_{t}\u003dku_{{xx}}\\, \\)  \\( u(0,t)\u003d0\\, \\) \n\u003cbr\u003e \\( u(l,t)\u003d0\\, \\) \n\u003cbr\u003e\n\u003cbr\u003e \\( u(x,0)\u003df(x)\\, \\) \n\u003cbr\u003e\n\u003cbr\u003e\n\u003cbr\u003e \n\u003cp\u003eFirst separate variables and plug back into the original equation.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( u(x,t)\u003dX(x)T(t)\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( XT\u0027\u003dkX\u0027\u0027T\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFind the separated boundary conditions (worry about the initial condition later).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( X(0)\u003dX(l)\u003d0\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNow seperate the two functions on either side of the equation. The reasoning is that if the left side is a function of \\( t \\) and it is equal to the right side, which is a function of \\( x \\) , then both sides of the equation must be equal to a constant. It\u0027s good to keep higher derivatives on top of lower ones, and keep the \\( k \\) with \\( T(t) \\) . When setting the next part equal to a constant, \\( -\\lambda \\) works best.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( {\\frac {T\u0027}{kT}}\u003d{\\frac {X\u0027\u0027}{X}}\u003d-\\lambda \\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis gives the two solutions to the ODEs:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( T(t)\u003dc_{1}e^{{-\\lambda kt}}\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( X(x)\u003dc_{2}\\cos({\\sqrt {\\lambda }}x)+c_{3}{\\frac {\\sin({\\sqrt {\\lambda }}x)}{{\\sqrt {\\lambda }}}}\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn the solution of \\( X(x) \\) the extra square root of \\( \\lambda \\) was added in the denominator so that we won\u0027t have to make a special case for \\( \\lambda \u003d0\\, \\) , which does not give interesting solutions anyway.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse the separated boundary conditions on the function \\( X(x) \\) .\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( X(0)\u003dc_{2}\u003d0\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( X(l)\u003dc_{3}{\\frac {\\sin({\\sqrt {\\lambda }}l)}{{\\sqrt {\\lambda }}}}\u003d0\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNothing interesting would come from letting \\( c_{3}\u003d0\\, \\) , so \\( \\lambda _{n}\u003d{\\frac {n^{2}\\pi ^{2}}{l^{2}}},\\,\\,\\,n\u003d1,2,3,...\\, \\) . \\( n\\neq 0\\, \\) because \\( \\lambda \\neq 0\\, \\) . These values of lambda are the eigenvalues. The eigenfunctions are \\( \\sin({\\frac {n\\pi x}{l}}),\\,\\,\\,n\u003d1,2,3,...\\, \\) .\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor each value of n, a solution is then\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( u_{n}(x,t)\u003dc_{1}e^{{-\\lambda _{n}kt}}c_{3}{\\frac {\\sin({\\sqrt {\\lambda _{n}}}x)}{{\\sqrt {\\lambda _{n}}}}}\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUsing the principle of superposition, the formal solution is the sum of all possible solutions:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( u(x,t)\u003d\\sum _{{n\u003d1}}^{\\infty }u_{n}(x,t)\u003d\\sum _{{n\u003d1}}^{\\infty }A_{n}e^{{-\\lambda _{n}kt}}\\sin({\\frac {n\\pi x}{l}}),A_{n}\u003d{\\frac {c_{1}c_{3}}{{\\frac {n\\pi }{l}}}}\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe initial condition gives\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( u(x,0)\u003df(x)\u003d\\sum _{{n\u003d1}}^{\\infty }A_{n}\\sin({\\frac {n\\pi x}{l}})\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis series is the Fourier sine series of \\( f(x) \\) , so the coefficient is given by\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( A_{n}\u003d{\\frac {2}{l}}\\int _{0}^{l}f(x)\\sin({\\frac {n\\pi x}{l}})\\,dx\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSo the final answer is\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( u(x,t)\u003d\\sum _{{n\u003d1}}^{\\infty }A_{n}e^{{-\\left({\\frac {n\\pi }{l}}\\right)^{2}kt}}\\sin({\\frac {n\\pi x}{l}}),\\,\\,\\,A_{n}\u003d{\\frac {2}{l}}\\int _{0}^{l}f(x)\\sin({\\frac {n\\pi x}{l}})\\,dx\\, \\) )\\sin({\\frac {n\\pi \\xi }{l}})\\,d\\xi \\right]e^{{-\\left({\\frac {n\\pi }{l}}\\right)^{2}kt}}\\sin({\\frac {n\\pi x}{l}})\\, \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e
